22	BoundingBox  bounds      # 2D bounding box containing map
23	
24	WayPoint[]   points      # way-points
25	MapFeature[] features    # map features
26	KeyValue[]   props       # map properties
27	
28	================================================================================
29	MSG: std_msgs/Header
30	# Standard metadata for higher-level stamped data types.
31	# This is generally used to communicate timestamped data 
32	# in a particular coordinate frame.
33	# 
34	# sequence ID: consecutively increasing ID 
35	uint32 seq
36	#Two-integer timestamp that is expressed as:
37	# * stamp.sec: seconds (stamp_secs) since epoch (in Python the variable is called 'secs')
38	# * stamp.nsec: nanoseconds since stamp_secs (in Python the variable is called 'nsecs')
39	# time-handling sugar is provided by the client library
40	time stamp
41	#Frame this data is associated with
42	string frame_id
43	
44	================================================================================
45	MSG: uuid_msgs/UniqueID
46	# A universally unique identifier (UUID).
47	#
48	#  http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universally_unique_identifier
49	#  http://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc4122.html
50	
51	uint8[16] uuid
52	
53	================================================================================
54	MSG: geographic_msgs/BoundingBox
55	# Geographic map bounding box. 
56	#
57	# The two GeoPoints denote diagonally opposite corners of the box.
58	#
59	# If min_pt.latitude is NaN, the bounding box is "global", matching
60	# any valid latitude, longitude and altitude.
61	#
62	# If min_pt.altitude is NaN, the bounding box is two-dimensional and
63	# matches any altitude within the specified latitude and longitude
64	# range.
65	
66	GeoPoint min_pt         # lowest and most Southwestern corner
67	GeoPoint max_pt         # highest and most Northeastern corner
68	
69	================================================================================
70	MSG: geographic_msgs/GeoPoint
71	# Geographic point, using the WGS 84 reference ellipsoid.
72	
73	# Latitude [degrees]. Positive is north of equator; negative is south
74	# (-90 <= latitude <= +90).
75	float64 latitude
76	
77	# Longitude [degrees]. Positive is east of prime meridian; negative is
78	# west (-180 <= longitude <= +180). At the poles, latitude is -90 or
79	# +90, and longitude is irrelevant, but must be in range.
80	float64 longitude
81	
82	# Altitude [m]. Positive is above the WGS 84 ellipsoid (NaN if unspecified).
83	float64 altitude
84	
85	================================================================================
86	MSG: geographic_msgs/WayPoint
87	# Way-point element for a geographic map.
88	
89	uuid_msgs/UniqueID id   # Unique way-point identifier
90	GeoPoint   position     # Position relative to WGS 84 ellipsoid
91	KeyValue[] props        # Key/value properties for this point
92	
93	================================================================================
94	MSG: geographic_msgs/KeyValue
95	# Geographic map tag (key, value) pair
96	#
97	# This is equivalent to diagnostic_msgs/KeyValue, repeated here to
98	# avoid introducing a trivial stack dependency.
99	
100	string key                     # tag label
101	string value                   # corresponding value
102	
103	================================================================================
104	MSG: geographic_msgs/MapFeature
105	# Geographic map feature.
106	#
107	# A list of WayPoint IDs for features like streets, highways, hiking
108	# trails, the outlines of buildings and parking lots in sequential
109	# order.
110	#
111	# Feature lists may also contain other feature lists as members.
112	
113	uuid_msgs/UniqueID   id         # Unique feature identifier
114	uuid_msgs/UniqueID[] components # Sequence of feature components
115	KeyValue[] props                # Key/value properties for this feature
116	"""
117	  __slots__ = ['header','id','bounds','points','features','props']

   More Info: https://bandit.readthedocs.io/en/latest/plugins/b824_url_found.html
14	  _has_header = True #flag to mark the presence of a Header object
15	  _full_text = """# This message defines meta information for a camera. It should be in a
16	# camera namespace on topic "camera_info" and accompanied by up to five
17	# image topics named:
18	#
19	#   image_raw - raw data from the camera driver, possibly Bayer encoded
20	#   image            - monochrome, distorted
21	#   image_color      - color, distorted
22	#   image_rect       - monochrome, rectified
23	#   image_rect_color - color, rectified
24	#
25	# The image_pipeline contains packages (image_proc, stereo_image_proc)
26	# for producing the four processed image topics from image_raw and
27	# camera_info. The meaning of the camera parameters are described in
28	# detail at http://www.ros.org/wiki/image_pipeline/CameraInfo.
29	#
30	# The image_geometry package provides a user-friendly interface to
31	# common operations using this meta information. If you want to, e.g.,
32	# project a 3d point into image coordinates, we strongly recommend
33	# using image_geometry.
34	#
35	# If the camera is uncalibrated, the matrices D, K, R, P should be left
36	# zeroed out. In particular, clients may assume that K[0] == 0.0
37	# indicates an uncalibrated camera.
38	
39	#######################################################################
40	#                     Image acquisition info                          #
41	#######################################################################
42	
43	# Time of image acquisition, camera coordinate frame ID
44	Header header    # Header timestamp should be acquisition time of image
45	                 # Header frame_id should be optical frame of camera
46	                 # origin of frame should be optical center of camera
47	                 # +x should point to the right in the image
48	                 # +y should point down in the image
49	                 # +z should point into the plane of the image
50	
51	
52	#######################################################################
53	#                      Calibration Parameters                         #
54	#######################################################################
55	# These are fixed during camera calibration. Their values will be the #
56	# same in all messages until the camera is recalibrated. Note that    #
57	# self-calibrating systems may "recalibrate" frequently.              #
58	#                                                                     #
59	# The internal parameters can be used to warp a raw (distorted) image #
60	# to:                                                                 #
61	#   1. An undistorted image (requires D and K)                        #
62	#   2. A rectified image (requires D, K, R)                           #
63	# The projection matrix P projects 3D points into the rectified image.#
64	#######################################################################
65	
66	# The image dimensions with which the camera was calibrated. Normally
67	# this will be the full camera resolution in pixels.
68	uint32 height
69	uint32 width
70	
71	# The distortion model used. Supported models are listed in
72	# sensor_msgs/distortion_models.h. For most cameras, "plumb_bob" - a
73	# simple model of radial and tangential distortion - is sufficient.
74	string distortion_model
75	
76	# The distortion parameters, size depending on the distortion model.
77	# For "plumb_bob", the 5 parameters are: (k1, k2, t1, t2, k3).
78	float64[] D
79	
80	# Intrinsic camera matrix for the raw (distorted) images.
81	#     [fx  0 cx]
82	# K = [ 0 fy cy]
83	#     [ 0  0  1]
84	# Projects 3D points in the camera coordinate frame to 2D pixel
85	# coordinates using the focal lengths (fx, fy) and principal point
86	# (cx, cy).
87	float64[9]  K # 3x3 row-major matrix
88	
89	# Rectification matrix (stereo cameras only)
90	# A rotation matrix aligning the camera coordinate system to the ideal
91	# stereo image plane so that epipolar lines in both stereo images are
92	# parallel.
93	float64[9]  R # 3x3 row-major matrix
94	
95	# Projection/camera matrix
96	#     [fx'  0  cx' Tx]
97	# P = [ 0  fy' cy' Ty]
98	#     [ 0   0   1   0]
99	# By convention, this matrix specifies the intrinsic (camera) matrix
100	#  of the processed (rectified) image. That is, the left 3x3 portion
101	#  is the normal camera intrinsic matrix for the rectified image.
102	# It projects 3D points in the camera coordinate frame to 2D pixel
103	#  coordinates using the focal lengths (fx', fy') and principal point
104	#  (cx', cy') - these may differ from the values in K.
105	# For monocular cameras, Tx = Ty = 0. Normally, monocular cameras will
106	#  also have R = the identity and P[1:3,1:3] = K.
107	# For a stereo pair, the fourth column [Tx Ty 0]' is related to the
108	#  position of the optical center of the second camera in the first
109	#  camera's frame. We assume Tz = 0 so both cameras are in the same
110	#  stereo image plane. The first camera always has Tx = Ty = 0. For
111	#  the right (second) camera of a horizontal stereo pair, Ty = 0 and
112	#  Tx = -fx' * B, where B is the baseline between the cameras.
113	# Given a 3D point [X Y Z]', the projection (x, y) of the point onto
114	#  the rectified image is given by:
115	#  [u v w]' = P * [X Y Z 1]'
116	#         x = u / w
117	#         y = v / w
118	#  This holds for both images of a stereo pair.
119	float64[12] P # 3x4 row-major matrix
120	
121	
122	#######################################################################
123	#                      Operational Parameters                         #
124	#######################################################################
125	# These define the image region actually captured by the camera       #
126	# driver. Although they affect the geometry of the output image, they #
127	# may be changed freely without recalibrating the camera.             #
128	#######################################################################
129	
130	# Binning refers here to any camera setting which combines rectangular
131	#  neighborhoods of pixels into larger "super-pixels." It reduces the
132	#  resolution of the output image to
133	#  (width / binning_x) x (height / binning_y).
134	# The default values binning_x = binning_y = 0 is considered the same
135	#  as binning_x = binning_y = 1 (no subsampling).
136	uint32 binning_x
137	uint32 binning_y
138	
139	# Region of interest (subwindow of full camera resolution), given in
140	#  full resolution (unbinned) image coordinates. A particular ROI
141	#  always denotes the same window of pixels on the camera sensor,
142	#  regardless of binning settings.
143	# The default setting of roi (all values 0) is considered the same as
144	#  full resolution (roi.width = width, roi.height = height).
145	RegionOfInterest roi
146	
147	================================================================================
148	MSG: std_msgs/Header
149	# Standard metadata for higher-level stamped data types.
150	# This is generally used to communicate timestamped data 
151	# in a particular coordinate frame.
152	# 
153	# sequence ID: consecutively increasing ID 
154	uint32 seq
155	#Two-integer timestamp that is expressed as:
156	# * stamp.sec: seconds (stamp_secs) since epoch (in Python the variable is called 'secs')
157	# * stamp.nsec: nanoseconds since stamp_secs (in Python the variable is called 'nsecs')
158	# time-handling sugar is provided by the client library
159	time stamp
160	#Frame this data is associated with
161	string frame_id
162	
163	================================================================================
164	MSG: sensor_msgs/RegionOfInterest
165	# This message is used to specify a region of interest within an image.
166	#
167	# When used to specify the ROI setting of the camera when the image was
168	# taken, the height and width fields should either match the height and
169	# width fields for the associated image; or height = width = 0
170	# indicates that the full resolution image was captured.
171	
172	uint32 x_offset  # Leftmost pixel of the ROI
173	                 # (0 if the ROI includes the left edge of the image)
174	uint32 y_offset  # Topmost pixel of the ROI
175	                 # (0 if the ROI includes the top edge of the image)
176	uint32 height    # Height of ROI
177	uint32 width     # Width of ROI
178	
179	# True if a distinct rectified ROI should be calculated from the "raw"
180	# ROI in this message. Typically this should be False if the full image
181	# is captured (ROI not used), and True if a subwindow is captured (ROI
182	# used).
183	bool do_rectify
184	"""
185	  __slots__ = ['header','height','width','distortion_model','D','K','R','P','binning_x','binning_y','roi']

51	uint8 REJECTED        = 5   # The goal was rejected by the action server without being processed,
52	                            #    because the goal was unattainable or invalid (Terminal State)
53	uint8 PREEMPTING      = 6   # The goal received a cancel request after it started executing
54	                            #    and has not yet completed execution
55	uint8 RECALLING       = 7   # The goal received a cancel request before it started executing,
56	                            #    but the action server has not yet confirmed that the goal is canceled
57	uint8 RECALLED        = 8   # The goal received a cancel request before it started executing
58	                            #    and was successfully cancelled (Terminal State)
59	uint8 LOST            = 9   # An action client can determine that a goal is LOST. This should not be
60	                            #    sent over the wire by an action server
61	
62	#Allow for the user to associate a string with GoalStatus for debugging
63	string text
64	
65	
66	================================================================================
67	MSG: actionlib_msgs/GoalID
68	# The stamp should store the time at which this goal was requested.
69	# It is used by an action server when it tries to preempt all
70	# goals that were requested before a certain time
71	time stamp
72	
73	# The id provides a way to associate feedback and
74	# result message with specific goal requests. The id
75	# specified must be unique.
76	string id
77	
78	
79	================================================================================
80	MSG: tf2_msgs/LookupTransformResult
81	# ====== DO NOT MODIFY! AUTOGENERATED FROM AN ACTION DEFINITION ======
82	geometry_msgs/TransformStamped transform
83	tf2_msgs/TF2Error error
84	
85	================================================================================
86	MSG: geometry_msgs/TransformStamped
87	# This expresses a transform from coordinate frame header.frame_id
88	# to the coordinate frame child_frame_id
89	#
90	# This message is mostly used by the 
91	# <a href="http://wiki.ros.org/tf">tf</a> package. 
92	# See its documentation for more information.
93	
94	Header header
95	string child_frame_id # the frame id of the child frame
96	Transform transform
97	
98	================================================================================
99	MSG: geometry_msgs/Transform
100	# This represents the transform between two coordinate frames in free space.
101	
102	Vector3 translation
103	Quaternion rotation
104	
105	================================================================================
106	MSG: geometry_msgs/Vector3
107	# This represents a vector in free space. 
108	# It is only meant to represent a direction. Therefore, it does not
109	# make sense to apply a translation to it (e.g., when applying a 
110	# generic rigid transformation to a Vector3, tf2 will only apply the
111	# rotation). If you want your data to be translatable too, use the
112	# geometry_msgs/Point message instead.
113	
114	float64 x
115	float64 y
116	float64 z
117	================================================================================
118	MSG: geometry_msgs/Quaternion
119	# This represents an orientation in free space in quaternion form.
120	
121	float64 x
122	float64 y
123	float64 z
124	float64 w
125

132	uint8 INVALID_ARGUMENT_ERROR = 4
133	uint8 TIMEOUT_ERROR = 5
134	uint8 TRANSFORM_ERROR = 6
135	
136	uint8 error
137	string error_string
138	"""

83	MSG: visualization_msgs/MenuEntry
84	# MenuEntry message.
85	
86	# Each InteractiveMarker message has an array of MenuEntry messages.
87	# A collection of MenuEntries together describe a
88	# menu/submenu/subsubmenu/etc tree, though they are stored in a flat
89	# array.  The tree structure is represented by giving each menu entry
90	# an ID number and a "parent_id" field.  Top-level entries are the
91	# ones with parent_id = 0.  Menu entries are ordered within their
92	# level the same way they are ordered in the containing array.  Parent
93	# entries must appear before their children.
94	
95	# Example:
96	# - id = 3
97	#   parent_id = 0
98	#   title = "fun"
99	# - id = 2
100	#   parent_id = 0
101	#   title = "robot"
102	# - id = 4
103	#   parent_id = 2
104	#   title = "pr2"
105	# - id = 5
106	#   parent_id = 2
107	#   title = "turtle"
108	#
109	# Gives a menu tree like this:
110	#  - fun
111	#  - robot
112	#    - pr2
113	#    - turtle
114	
115	# ID is a number for each menu entry.  Must be unique within the
116	# control, and should never be 0.
117	uint32 id
118	
119	# ID of the parent of this menu entry, if it is a submenu.  If this
120	# menu entry is a top-level entry, set parent_id to 0.
121	uint32 parent_id
122	
123	# menu / entry title
124	string title
125	
126	# Arguments to command indicated by command_type (below)
127	string command
128	
129	# Command_type stores the type of response desired when this menu
130	# entry is clicked.
131	# FEEDBACK: send an InteractiveMarkerFeedback message with menu_entry_id set to this entry's id.
132	# ROSRUN: execute "rosrun" with arguments given in the command field (above).
133	# ROSLAUNCH: execute "roslaunch" with arguments given in the command field (above).
134	uint8 FEEDBACK=0
135	uint8 ROSRUN=1
136	uint8 ROSLAUNCH=2
137	uint8 command_type

171	# MOVE_PLANE: Translate in local y-z plane.
172	# ROTATE_AXIS: Rotate around local x-axis.
173	# MOVE_ROTATE: Combines MOVE_PLANE and ROTATE_AXIS.
174	uint8 NONE = 0 
175	uint8 MENU = 1

183	# ROTATE_3D: Rotate freely in 3D space about the origin of parent frame.

185	uint8 MOVE_3D = 7
186	uint8 ROTATE_3D = 8
187	uint8 MOVE_ROTATE_3D = 9
188

195	
196	
197	# Markers to be displayed as custom visual representation.
198	# Leave this empty to use the default control handles.
199	#
200	# Note: 
201	# - The markers can be defined in an arbitrary coordinate frame,
202	#   but will be transformed into the local frame of the interactive marker.
203	# - If the header of a marker is empty, its pose will be interpreted as 
204	#   relative to the pose of the parent interactive marker.
205	Marker[] markers
206	
207

104	# A collection of MenuEntries together describe a
105	# menu/submenu/subsubmenu/etc tree, though they are stored in a flat
106	# array.  The tree structure is represented by giving each menu entry
107	# an ID number and a "parent_id" field.  Top-level entries are the

109	# level the same way they are ordered in the containing array.  Parent

125	#

127	#  - fun

130	#    - turtle
